## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), which is the standard first-order state-space form of an oscillator x' = v, v' = f(x,v,t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly combine restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear spring-mass motion)
- Linear viscous damping + linear restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with external drive: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear resonance)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * Abs(v) * v - c1 * x (aerodynamic-like damping plus spring restoring)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (smoothed sign(v) friction in oscillators)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle (sinusoidal restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * sin(x) (rotational oscillator with gravity restoring torque)
- Driven pendulum: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * sin(x) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically forced pendulum/phase locking)
- van der Pol oscillator (self-excited nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (limit-cycle oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (self-oscillation via negative damping at small |v|)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Piecewise/saturating stiffness (hard stop / cubic-like via abs): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * Abs(x) * x (nonlinear spring stiffening with displacement magnitude)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (odd restoring), with little/no explicit t or v dependence; implies near energy conservation and closed orbits in (x,v).
- Viscous damping signature: a term proportional to -v; causes amplitude decay and spiraling trajectories toward the origin in phase space.
- Quadratic/aerodynamic damping signature: terms like -Abs(v)*v; decay rate increases with speed, producing faster damping at large amplitudes than near equilibrium.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior: damping that changes sign with amplitude (e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v) yields growth from small motions and saturation to a finite oscillation.
- Geometric (pendulum-like) restoring: sin(x) indicates periodic potential and bounded torque; for small x it approximates linear restoring, while at larger x it softens and can enable rotational regimes.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: +x**3 in restoring (implemented via -c*x - c*x**3 in dv_dt) shifts frequency upward with amplitude (hardening) or downward (softening) depending on sign of the cubic term.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin/cos terms in t produce resonance tongues, entrainment, and possibly chaos when combined with nonlinearity (e.g., Duffing, driven pendulum).
- Parametric forcing: multiplicative time dependence on x (e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) produces parametric resonance distinct from additive forcing and often exhibits instability bands.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO17)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x
Candidate formulas: 88

GT (fixed):
\[
-0.2634379499\,v\sin(x)\;-\;0.5268758999\,v\;-\;2.5071295689\,x\;+\;0.4607662803\,\sin(t).
\]
So GT has exactly these functional components:
1) linear in \(x\): \((-2.5071)x\)  
2) linear in \(v\): \((-0.5269)v\)  
3) mixed term \(v\sin(x)\) with coefficient \(-0.2634\)  
4) pure time sinusoid \(\sin(t)\) with amplitude \(0.4608\)  
and **no** constants, no exponentials, no logs, no powers, no \(|\cdot|\), no Max, no \(x^3\), etc.

Key trig rewrite needed for candidates: \(v\cos(x+\phi)\) can equal \(v\sin(x)\) by choosing \(\phi=-\pi/2\) since \(\cos(x-\pi/2)=\sin(x)\). Also \(\cos(t+\phi)\) can equal \(\sin(t)\) by \(\phi=-\pi/2\).

Now check each candidate for whether we can set parameters to get *exactly* those four terms and kill everything else.

---

### 1. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2\cos(c3 t+c4)+ c5 v\cos(c6+x)+ c7 e^{c8 t}\cos(c9+x)\)
Has an extra \(e^{c8 t}\cos(\cdot)\) term depending on \(t\) and \(x\). Only way to remove it for all \((t,x)\) is set \(c7=0\). Then we can match:
- \(c0 v\) to \(-0.5268758999 v\)
- \(c1 x\) to \(-2.5071295689 x\)
- \(c2\cos(c3 t+c4)\) to \(0.4607662803\sin(t)\) via \(c3=1,\;c4=-\pi/2,\;c2=0.4607662803\)
- \(c5 v\cos(c6+x)\) to \(-0.2634379499 v\sin(x)\) via \(c6=-\pi/2,\;c5=-0.2634379499\)
So **matches**.

### 2. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2 + c3\cos(c4 t+c5)+ c6 e^{c7 t}+ c8 v\cos(c9+x)\)
Extra constant \(c2\) and extra pure exponential \(c6 e^{c7 t}\). Set \(c2=0,\;c6=0\). Remaining terms can match exactly as in (1) (use cosine phase shifts for \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(x)\)). **Matches**.

### 3. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2 + c3 t^{c4}+ c5\cos(c6 t+c7)+ c8 v\cos(c9+x)\)
Extra constant \(c2\) and extra power term \(c3 t^{c4}\). Set \(c2=0,\;c3=0\). Then match cosine terms as before. **Matches**.

### 4. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2\sin(c3 t+c4)+ c5\cos(c6 t+c7)+ c8 v\cos(c9+x)\)
Has *two* independent time sinusoids (a sine and a cosine). GT has only one sinusoid. We can set one amplitude to 0, e.g. \(c5=0\). Then choose \(c3=1,c4=0\) and \(c2=0.4607662803\) to get \(\sin(t)\). And choose \(c8,c9\) to get \(v\sin(x)\) via cosine phase shift; choose \(c0,c1\) for linear terms. **Matches**.

### 5. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2\cos(c3 t+c4)+ c5 v\cos(c6+x)+ c7\cos(c8 t+c9)\)
Two time cosines; set \(c7=0\). Then identical structure to (1) without exponential. **Matches**.

**GT: -0.263437949946663*v*sin(x) - 0.526875899893326*v - 2.50712956886133*x + 0.460766280298364*sin(t)**

This can be rewritten as:
- A term proportional to `v` (linear in v)
- A term proportional to `x` (linear in x)
- A term proportional to `v*sin(x)`
- A term proportional to `sin(t)`

Note that `v*sin(x) = -v*cos(x + π/2)`, so `v*cos(c + x)` with appropriate constant can represent `v*sin(x)`.

Also, `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(c3*t + c4)` with `c3=1` can represent `sin(t)`.

The GT has **no constant term** (no additive constant), **no exponential terms**, **no log terms**, **no power terms**, **no v² or v³ terms**, **no x² or x³ terms**, **no t terms**, etc.

The key structure is: `c*v + c*x + c*cos(t + phase) + c*v*cos(x + phase)`

**Candidate 41:** `c0*v + c1*x + c2*cos(c3*t + c4) + c5*v*cos(c6 + x) + c7*Max(0, c8*v) + c7*Max(0, c9*v)`
The two Max terms share coefficient c7. If c8>0 and c9<0, then c7*Max(0,c8*v)+c7*Max(0,c9*v) = c7*(c8*Max(0,v) + |c9|*Max(0,-v)). This equals c7*c8*v when v>0 and -c7*|c9|*v when v<0. For this to equal a linear function of v (like adding to c0*v), we need c8=|c9|, giving c7*c8*|v|. But |v| ≠ v since v takes both signs. However, if c7=0, the Max terms vanish. ✓
